Refutation of Those Who Attach Existence to Power Without Creation
Comparison of two errors regarding divine attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why attaching existence to God's power alone (without the act of bringing into existence) is a graver error than the Karamiyya's linguistic mistake, because it denies the reality of divine attributes.

Core Idea
Attaching existence to power alone is far worse than a mere metaphor.

In this passage, the author compares two theological errors to emphasize the severity of denying the real meaning of divine creative attributes. The Karamiyya mistakenly treat a permissible metaphor as literal truth, but those who attach existence to power without an act of creation commit a deeper ignorance: they attach to God's power something that is not proper to it, reducing terms like ījād and takwīn to empty words.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two groups criticized
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that the author criticizes two groups: the Karamiyya and those who attach existence to power without ījād.
The passage begins with 'Then the ignorance...' signaling a comparison.
2
Understand the Karamiyya error
The Karamiyya affirm the name 'Creator' based on power alone without the attribute of creation. The author says this is an error about expressions (ʿibārāt), taking a metaphor as reality.
This is described as 'one ignorance in expressions'.
3
Understand the worse error
The other group attaches existence itself to power without ījād or takwīn, treating these terms as meaningless. This is like attaching existence to knowledge or sight, which is impossible.
This is described as 'two ignorances concerning realities'.
4
Compare the two errors
Contrast the two: one is a linguistic mistake (metaphor taken as reality), the other is a mistake about realities (attaching an improper property to power). The latter is more severe.
The comparison highlights the importance of affirming real divine attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم جهالة من يعلق الوجود بالقدرة دون الإيجاد أفحش من جهالة الكرامية حيث يثبتون اسم الخالق بالقدرة دون صفة الخلق لأن ذلك من باب العبارات، وقد يوجد مثل ذلك في الشاهد وإن كان مجازا فجهالتهم أنهم ظنوا المجاز حقيقة، وهؤلاء علقوا بحقيقة القدرة ما لا يصلح حكما لها، فصاروا كمن علق الوجود بالعلم أو السمع أو البصر، وذلك محال فكذا هذا، وجعلوا الإيجاد والتكوين عبارتين فارغتين عن المعنى. فإذا هاتان جهالتان في الحقائق، وتلك جهالة واحدة في محال العبارات.
Then the ignorance of one who attaches existence to power without bringing into existence (ījād) is worse than the ignorance of the Karāmiyya, who affirm the name 'Creator' based on power without the attribute of creation (khalq), because that belongs to the realm of expressions; and such may be found in the witnessed world even if metaphorical. So their ignorance is that they took the metaphor as reality. And these (here) attached to the reality of power something that is not a proper property of it; they became like one who attaches existence to knowledge or hearing or sight, and that is impossible, so likewise this. And they made 'bringing into existence' (ījād) and 'making' (takwīn) two expressions empty of meaning. Thus these are two ignorances concerning realities, while that (of the Karāmiyya) is a single ignorance in the realm of expressions.
Source pages p. 537

Commentary
This passage compares two errors. The Karāmiyya mistakenly think that the name 'Creator' (khāliq) can be applied based solely on power (qudra) without the attribute of creation (khalq). The author notes that this is about linguistic usage (ʿibārāt); in worldly analogy, such a metaphor might be permissible, but the Karāmiyya took a metaphor as literal truth, which is one ignorance. However, the error of those who attach existence to power (without ījād) is far worse: they attach to the reality of power something that does not belong to it as a property. This is like attaching existence to knowledge, hearing, or sight – all impossible. Furthermore, they treat ījād and takwīn as empty words, devoid of meaning. Thus, these people commit two acts of ignorance about realities, while the Karāmiyya commit only one ignorance about expressions. The passage highlights the severity of denying the real meaning of divine creative attributes.

قدرة
إيجاد
تكوين
كرامية

مجاز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that ascribing creation to God's power alone (without an act of takwīn) is acceptable if it is a metaphor, just as the Karāmiyya did.
Correction: The author argues that attaching existence to power without ījād is not merely a metaphorical mistake; it is a denial of the reality of divine attributes, and is far more severe.

Checkpoint
According to the author, how many ignorances are committed by those who attach existence to power without ījād compared to the Karāmiyya?
A) One ignorance in realities.
B) Two ignorances in realities.
C) One ignorance in expressions.
D) Two ignorances in expressions.

Key Takeaway
Denying the real meaning of creative attributes (ījād/takwīn) is a more fundamental error than misusing a metaphor about divine names.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

When you recall God's attribute of power (qudra), do you instinctively connect it to His actual act of creating things, or do you treat it as a vague concept? The author warns against making 'ījād' and 'takwīn' empty words—are there divine attributes you have reduced to mere labels without engaging their reality? Write one attribute you will strive to understand more deeply this week.
?
The author says the second group committed 'two ignorances concerning realities'. If you are honest, how many 'ignorances' might you hold about God's attributes—comfortable metaphors you have mistaken for truth? Identify one belief about God that you have accepted without grounding it in the reality of what the Qur'an and Sunnah teach, and commit to studying it with a teacher.
?
Imagine standing before Allah on the Day of Judgment and being asked about your understanding of His creation. Would you confess that you settled for a shallow metaphor, or can you say you strove to grasp the reality of takwīn? What step will you take today to move from metaphor to truth in your understanding of God's creative power?

Refuting the Ash'ari Doubt on Act and Createdness
Nasafi refutes the Ash'ari argument that kufr being an act and created implies acts can be created.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi response to the Ash'ari argument that an act being created implies the act can be created by the servant.

Core Idea
An act can be the servant's doing without being created by him.

The Ash'ari school sometimes argued that if an act like kufr is both a servant's act and created, then acts can be created. The Maturidi response is subtle: the act is the servant's but creation is Allah's alone. This passage unpacks that distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Get a feel for the argument before diving into commentary.
Notice the structure: Ash'ari claim, then Nasafi's response.
2
Identify the Ash'ari doubt
The Ash'ari claim is that since kufr is both an act (fi'l) of the servant and a created thing (maf'ul), it is permissible for an act to be a created thing (i.e., the servant can create his own act). Identify this claim in the text.
3
Understand Nasafi's refutation
Nasafi denies the premise by distinguishing between 'act' and 'created thing.' He says kufr is the servant's act but not his created thing; it is Allah's creation. Grasp this key distinction.
The Arabic: 'بل الكفر فعله لا مفعول وهو مفعول الله تعالى.'
4
Recognize the rejection of consensus
Nasafi rejects the idea that what is not created by the servant cannot be his act. He calls this false and notes that opponents do not agree. This is crucial for defending human agency without compromising divine creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[شبهة أخرى والرد عليها] وأما ما قال غيره من الأشعرية : إن الكفر فعل العبد وهو مفعول فدل ذلك على جواز كون الفعل مفعولا فالجواب أن هذا غير مسلم بل الكفر فعله لا مفعول وهو مفعول الله تعالى، ومن ادعى من الاتفاق أن ما ليس بمفعول للعبد ليس بفعل له، باطل وخصومه لا يوافقونه في ذلك، وقد أقمنا الدلالة على كون وجوب الفعل غير المفعول.
[Another doubt and its refutation] As for what others among the Ash'ariyya said: that kufr (disbelief) is an act of the servant and it is a created thing (maf'ul), so that indicates the permissibility of an act being a created thing. The answer is that this is not granted; rather, kufr is his act, not a created thing (by him), and it is a created thing of Allah Most High. And whoever claims by consensus that what is not a created thing by the servant is not an act of his is false, and his opponents do not agree with him in that. And we have established the evidence that the necessity of the act is other than the created thing.
Source pages p. 542

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an Ash'ari doubt regarding the relationship between an act and its being created. The Ash'ari argument is that since kufr (disbelief) is both an act of the servant and a created thing (by Allah), therefore it is permissible for an act to be a created thing. Nasafi responds by denying the premise: kufr is indeed an act of the servant, but it is not a created thing in the sense that the servant creates it; rather, it is created by Allah. The servant's act does not cease to be his act simply because it is created by Allah. He then refutes the claim that there is a consensus that what is not created by the servant cannot be his act, stating that this is false and not agreed upon. Finally, he asserts that they have already provided evidence that the necessary existence of the act (wujub al-fi'l) is distinct from the created thing (maf'ul), implying that an act can be attributed to the agent while being brought into existence by Allah.

Key Terms
فعل
مفعول
كفر
عبد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If an act is a created thing, then the one who performs it must have created it.
Correction: An act can be performed by the servant while being created by Allah; creation and performance are distinct.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, how does he refute the Ash'ari claim that kufr being an act and a created thing proves that acts can be created?
A) He denies that kufr is an act of the servant.
B) He affirms that kufr is the servant's act but not his created thing, and is created by Allah.
C) He argues that kufr is neither an act nor a created thing.
D) He accepts the Ash'ari premise but denies the conclusion.

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi position distinguishes between the act (fi'l) as the servant's responsibility and the creation (maf'ul) as Allah's act.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you ever catch yourself thinking, 'It wasn't really my fault because Allah created it'? How does Nasafi's distinction between fi‘l (your act) and maf‘ūl (Allah's creation) challenge you to take full ownership of your actions? Will you, from now on, repent without excuses, knowing that your sin is truly yours while Allah created it?
?
Have you ever accepted a belief simply because 'everyone says so' or claimed a consensus to avoid deeper thinking? This passage exposes a false claim of consensus. Where in your life might you be relying on a false consensus to justify your views or actions? How can you test your beliefs against the Quran and Sunnah instead?
?
This lesson teaches that your actions are your responsibility even though Allah creates them. Do you truly live with this tension, or do you lean too far toward fatalism or self-reliance? What specific situation in your life right now requires you to embrace both divine decree and your own accountability? Commit to one concrete step you will take today to act in light of this truth.

The First Refutation: Takwin by Power Implies Eternal Ījād
Al-Nasafi presents the first two logical refutations of the Karamiyya view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Karamiyya claim that takwin is originated by power alone logically entails that bringing into existence (ījād) is eternal, destroying their own position.

Core Idea
If takwin is by power alone, then power itself is takwin — and an eternal power entails an eternal act.

Al-Nasafi begins his refutation by examining the internal logic of the Karamiyya doctrine. They claim that takwin is originated in God's essence by His eternal power, without any further act of creation. But as we shall see, this assumption leads to a chain of contradictions that undermine their entire theology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Karamiyya claim
Read the first part of the passage where al-Nasafi states the Karamiyya position: that takwin is originated by power, not by another act of bringing into existence.
Note that they distinguish between takwin and iḥdāth.
2
Follow the first argument
Al-Nasafi argues that if takwin were by power, then power would be takwin, because takwin is that by which things come to be. Since power is eternal, this would make ījād eternal.
This is a reductio ad absurdum: an eternal ījād contradicts the temporality of the world.
3
Consider the second argument
The second argument states that if an act could occur by mere power without takwin, then the world could exist without being caused to be originated (muhdath). This would invalidate the need for takwin altogether.
Both arguments show that the Karamiyya position leads to self-contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس يستقيم قول الكرامية إنه محدث بالقدرة، إذ من مذهبهم أن التكوين محدث في ذات الباري تعالى بقدرته لا بإحداث وتكوين، ثم يحدث جميع العالم بتكوين الله تعالى القائم بذاته لأن هذا فاسد من وجوه أحدها أنه لو كان بالقدرة لكانت القدرة تكوينا، لأن التكوين ليس إلا ما يتكون به المكون وكذا الإيجاد ليس إلا يوجد به الحادث، فإذا كان هذا في الحقيقة قولا بقدم الإيجاد، لأن القدرة عندهم أزلية، ولأن حدوث الفعل لو جاز بمجرد القدرة من غير الإيجاد والتكوين لجاز ذلك في جميع العالم فيكون العالم حادثا غير محدث موجودا بالقدرة، فيبطل القول بوجود التكوين، فيبطل القول بحدوثه بالقدرة، فيكون هذا أيضا قولا يوجب صحة بطلانه، وما هذا سبيله من الأقاويل فهو باطل. ولأن عندهم حدوث التكوين بالقدرة وحدوث جميع العالم بالتكوين، فيسمون التكوين حادثا لا محدثا، لأنه ما حدث بالإحداث ليكون محدثا ويسمون العالم محدثا لأن حدوثه كان بالإحداث، ويقولون المحدث ما وقع عليه الإحداث، فأما [؟] حادث لم يقع عليه الإحداث فهو ليس بمحدث. وكذا يسمون كلام الله تعالى حادثا لا محدثا مخلوقا، فكان التكوين هو مقدور الله تعالى لا غير وهو حادث في ذاته، والعالم ليس بمقدور الله فلم تكن الله تعالى قدرة إلا على ما في ذاته فأما على وراء ذلك فلا قدرة له عليه. وهذا فاسد من وجوده لما فيه من إزالة قدرة الله تعالى عن العالم واقتصار قدرته على ما في ذاته والقول به مما يوجب مسارعة العقلاء أجمع إلى إكفارهم، ولأن القول به إنكار لقوله تعالى: {وَهُوَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ} وعندهم لا يقدر على شيء إلا على ما حدث في ذاته، ولأن من أجزاء العالم ما هو مقدور غير الله تعالى وهو أفعال الحيوانات أجمع فلو لم تكن مقدورة له مع جواز كونها مقدورة لغيره للزمه العجز.
And the statement of the Karāmiyya is not sound—that it (i.e., takwin) is originated by power, for their doctrine is that takwin is originated in the essence of the Creator Most High by His power, not by an act of bringing into existence (iḥdāth) and takwin, then He originates the entire world by the takwin of God Most High that subsists in His essence—because this is corrupt in several respects. One of them is that if it were by power, then power would be takwin, because takwin is nothing but that by which the thing brought into existence comes to be, and similarly bringing into existence (ījād) is nothing but that by which the originated thing exists. So this would in reality be a statement of the eternity of bringing into existence, because power in their view is eternal. And because if the occurrence of the act were permissible merely by power without bringing into existence and takwin, then that would be permissible for the entire world, so the world would be originated (ḥādith) but not caused to be originated (muhdath), existing by power. That would invalidate the statement of the existence of takwin, and would invalidate the statement of its being originated by power. So this too is a statement whose soundness necessitates its own falsehood, and whatever sayings are of this way are false. And because in their view, the occurrence of takwin is by power, and the occurrence of the entire world is by takwin; they call takwin 'originated (ḥādith)' but not 'caused to be originated (muhdath),' because it did not occur by an act of bringing into existence so as to be muhdath. And they call the world 'muhdath' because its occurrence was by an act of bringing into existence. And they say: 'Al-muhdath is that which the act of bringing into existence falls upon; as for a ḥādith upon which the act of bringing into existence has not fallen, it is not muhdath.' Similarly, they call the speech of God Most High 'ḥādith' but not 'muhdath' nor 'created' (makhluq). So takwin is that which is within God's power only, and it is originated in His essence, while the world is not within God's power; thus God Most High has power only over what is in His essence; as for anything beyond that, He has no power over it. And this is corrupt from its very existence due to what it contains of removing God's power over the world and restricting His power to what is in His essence. And holding this statement necessitates that all rational people hasten to declare them disbelievers. And because holding it is a denial of His saying Most High: {And He is over all things powerful}, while in their view He is not capable of anything except what occurs in His essence. And because among the parts of the world are things that are within the power of other than God Most High, namely all the actions of animals; so if they were not within His power while it is possible for them to be within the power of another, then incapability (al-ʿajz) would be necessary for Him.
Source pages p. 543

Commentary
This passage is a detailed refutation of the Karamiyya theological sect's position regarding al-takwin (the act of bringing into existence). The Karamiyya claim that takwin is originated (ḥādith) in God's essence by His power (qudra) without needing a separate act of bringing into existence (iḥdāth) or another takwin. Then, through this takwin that subsists in God's essence, the entire world is originated. Al-Nasafi gives several reasons why this position is corrupt. First, if takwin were by power alone, then power itself would be takwin, because takwin is that by which things come to be. Since power is eternal in their view, this would imply that bringing into existence (ījād) is eternal—a contradiction because they affirm that the world is originated. Second, if an act could occur by mere power without an act of creating, then the whole world could come about by power alone, negating the need for a distinct act of takwin. This would make the world exist by power without being caused to be originated (muhdath), which they themselves reject. Third, the Karamiyya distinguish between ḥādith (originated) and muhdath (caused to be originated): they call takwin ḥādith but not muhdath, because it is not brought into existence by an act of creation; the world, however, is muhdath. This leads to the conclusion that God's power extends only to what occurs in His essence (i.e., takwin) and not to the world itself—a severe limitation that contradicts the Qur'anic verse 'He is over all things powerful' (Q. 30:50). Moreover, it implies that God is incapable (ʿajz) with respect to the actions of animals, which are within the power of other agents. Al-Nasafi concludes that this doctrine obliges all rational people to declare the Karamiyya disbelievers.

Key Terms
الكرامية
التكوين
القدرة
الإيجاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Nasafi's first argument, if takwin is by power, what does power become?
A) A separate attribute.
B) Takwin itself.
C) The world.
D) A created thing.

Key Takeaway
The Karamiyya position that takwin is originated by power alone collapses because it either eternalizes the act of creation or makes takwin superfluous.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever claim that your intentions are good enough, without actually following through with action? How does this lesson's argument about 'power without act' expose the emptiness of such a claim in your own life?
?
The Karamiyya held a seemingly subtle position that collapsed under logical scrutiny. What belief about God do you hold that you have never examined thoroughly? Will you test it today against the sources and reason?
?
If God's power alone sufficed for creation, then takwin is redundant. In your own life, are there areas where you rely on mere 'power' (ability, potential) instead of actual 'takwin' (bringing things into existence through action)? What step will you take today to move from potential to actual?

The Second Refutation: Limiting God's Power to His Essence
Al-Nasafi refutes the Karamiyya claim that God's power extends only to takwin in His essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Karamiyya distinction between ḥādith and muhdath leads to the blasphemous conclusion that God's power is restricted to His essence, contradicting the Qur'an and reason.

Core Idea
The Karamiyya restrict God's power to His essence, denying His omnipotence over the world.

Having shown the internal contradictions of the Karamiyya view, al-Nasafi now turns to its outrageous consequences. He demonstrates that their distinction between 'originated' (ḥādith) and 'caused to be originated' (muhdath) forces them to limit God's power exclusively to what occurs in His own essence—a position that the Qur'an explicitly denies and that all rational people must reject.

Guided Path
1
Understand the ḥādith/muhdath distinction
The Karamiyya distinguish between that which is originated but not caused to be originated (takwin) and that which is caused to be originated (the world). Read how they apply this to speech and takwin.
They call takwin 'ḥādith' but not 'muhdath'.
2
See the consequence for God's power
If takwin is the only thing originated in God's essence and it is not caused by another act, then God's power is limited to His essence. The world is beyond His power.
This is a severe restriction of divine omnipotence.
3
Consider the scriptural and rational refutation
Al-Nasafi cites the Qur'anic verse 'He is over all things powerful' and argues that if God cannot create the actions of animals (which are within the power of others), then He is incapable (ʿajz).
This is sufficient to declare the Karamiyya disbelievers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس يستقيم قول الكرامية إنه محدث بالقدرة، إذ من مذهبهم أن التكوين محدث في ذات الباري تعالى بقدرته لا بإحداث وتكوين، ثم يحدث جميع العالم بتكوين الله تعالى القائم بذاته لأن هذا فاسد من وجوه أحدها أنه لو كان بالقدرة لكانت القدرة تكوينا، لأن التكوين ليس إلا ما يتكون به المكون وكذا الإيجاد ليس إلا يوجد به الحادث، فإذا كان هذا في الحقيقة قولا بقدم الإيجاد، لأن القدرة عندهم أزلية، ولأن حدوث الفعل لو جاز بمجرد القدرة من غير الإيجاد والتكوين لجاز ذلك في جميع العالم فيكون العالم حادثا غير محدث موجودا بالقدرة، فيبطل القول بوجود التكوين، فيبطل القول بحدوثه بالقدرة، فيكون هذا أيضا قولا يوجب صحة بطلانه، وما هذا سبيله من الأقاويل فهو باطل. ولأن عندهم حدوث التكوين بالقدرة وحدوث جميع العالم بالتكوين، فيسمون التكوين حادثا لا محدثا، لأنه ما حدث بالإحداث ليكون محدثا ويسمون العالم محدثا لأن حدوثه كان بالإحداث، ويقولون المحدث ما وقع عليه الإحداث، فأما [؟] حادث لم يقع عليه الإحداث فهو ليس بمحدث. وكذا يسمون كلام الله تعالى حادثا لا محدثا مخلوقا، فكان التكوين هو مقدور الله تعالى لا غير وهو حادث في ذاته، والعالم ليس بمقدور الله فلم تكن الله تعالى قدرة إلا على ما في ذاته فأما على وراء ذلك فلا قدرة له عليه. وهذا فاسد من وجوده لما فيه من إزالة قدرة الله تعالى عن العالم واقتصار قدرته على ما في ذاته والقول به مما يوجب مسارعة العقلاء أجمع إلى إكفارهم، ولأن القول به إنكار لقوله تعالى: {وَهُوَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ} وعندهم لا يقدر على شيء إلا على ما حدث في ذاته، ولأن من أجزاء العالم ما هو مقدور غير الله تعالى وهو أفعال الحيوانات أجمع فلو لم تكن مقدورة له مع جواز كونها مقدورة لغيره للزمه العجز.
And the statement of the Karāmiyya is not sound—that it (i.e., takwin) is originated by power, for their doctrine is that takwin is originated in the essence of the Creator Most High by His power, not by an act of bringing into existence (iḥdāth) and takwin, then He originates the entire world by the takwin of God Most High that subsists in His essence—because this is corrupt in several respects. One of them is that if it were by power, then power would be takwin, because takwin is nothing but that by which the thing brought into existence comes to be, and similarly bringing into existence (ījād) is nothing but that by which the originated thing exists. So this would in reality be a statement of the eternity of bringing into existence, because power in their view is eternal. And because if the occurrence of the act were permissible merely by power without bringing into existence and takwin, then that would be permissible for the entire world, so the world would be originated (ḥādith) but not caused to be originated (muhdath), existing by power. That would invalidate the statement of the existence of takwin, and would invalidate the statement of its being originated by power. So this too is a statement whose soundness necessitates its own falsehood, and whatever sayings are of this way are false. And because in their view, the occurrence of takwin is by power, and the occurrence of the entire world is by takwin; they call takwin 'originated (ḥādith)' but not 'caused to be originated (muhdath),' because it did not occur by an act of bringing into existence so as to be muhdath. And they call the world 'muhdath' because its occurrence was by an act of bringing into existence. And they say: 'Al-muhdath is that which the act of bringing into existence falls upon; as for a ḥādith upon which the act of bringing into existence has not fallen, it is not muhdath.' Similarly, they call the speech of God Most High 'ḥādith' but not 'muhdath' nor 'created' (makhluq). So takwin is that which is within God's power only, and it is originated in His essence, while the world is not within God's power; thus God Most High has power only over what is in His essence; as for anything beyond that, He has no power over it. And this is corrupt from its very existence due to what it contains of removing God's power over the world and restricting His power to what is in His essence. And holding this statement necessitates that all rational people hasten to declare them disbelievers. And because holding it is a denial of His saying Most High: {And He is over all things powerful}, while in their view He is not capable of anything except what occurs in His essence. And because among the parts of the world are things that are within the power of other than God Most High, namely all the actions of animals; so if they were not within His power while it is possible for them to be within the power of another, then incapability (al-ʿajz) would be necessary for Him.

Commentary
This passage is a detailed refutation of the Karamiyya theological sect's position regarding al-takwin (the act of bringing into existence). The Karamiyya claim that takwin is originated (ḥādith) in God's essence by His power (qudra) without needing a separate act of bringing into existence (iḥdāth) or another takwin. Eternal Takwin Has Salaf Precedent
Refutes the objection by citing Imam Tahawi's creed affirming eternal takwin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the claim that the eternity of takwin is an innovation (hadith) with no basis among the Salaf by citing Imam Tahawi's creed.

Core Idea
Eternal takwin is not an innovation; it is rooted in the early Hanafi tradition.

In this passage, the author addresses a common objection against the Maturidi view on takwin: that it is a later innovation with no support from the early Muslims. He counters this by pointing to the renowned Hanafi scholar Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi, whose creedal work explicitly attributes the doctrine to the founding imams of the school. This refutation grounds the theological position in authoritative tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Read the first part of the passage to understand the opponent's claim: that the view of eternal takwin is a hadith (innovation) with no basis among the Salaf and no imam held it.
2
Examine the refutation
Notice how the author dismisses the objection as 'false' and 'born of ignorance of the schools of the Salaf.' This is a strong rebuttal.
3
Appreciate the evidence
The author cites Imam Tahawi's book al-'Aqa'id, where Tahawi states that his creed is that of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. This shows the view is not new.
Tahawi is a highly respected Hanafi scholar, so his testimony carries weight.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Although the quote is cut off, the intended conclusion is clear: the doctrine of eternal takwin has authentic precedent in the early Hanafi tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما ما زعموا أن هذا القول حادث لا أصل له في السلف ولا قائل به من الأئمة، فقول باطل صدر عن الجهل بمذاهب السلف، وذلك أن أبا جعفر الطحاوي وهو مما لا تخفى درجته وعلو رتبته في معرفة أقاويل سلف الأمة على العموم ومعرفة أقاويل أصحاب أبي حنيفة على الخصوص قال في كتابه المسمى بالعقائد الذي افتتحه فقال: صح عندي مذهب فقهاء الملة أبي حنيفة النعمان ابن ثابت الكوفي وأبي يوسف يعقوب بن إبراهيم الأنصاري وأبي عبد الله محمد
As for their claim that this saying is an innovation with no basis among the Salaf nor any proponent among the imams, this is a false statement arising from ignorance of the schools of the Salaf. That is because Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi—whose rank and eminence in knowledge of the sayings of the Salaf in general and knowledge of the sayings of the followers of Abu Hanifa in particular is not hidden—said in his book called al-'Aqa'id, which he began by saying: 'The doctrine of the jurists of the community, Abu Hanifa al-Nu'man ibn Thabit al-Kufi, Abu Yusuf Ya'qub ibn Ibrahim al-Ansari, and Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad...'.
Source pages p. 554

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection that the view of the eternity of takwin is an innovation (hadith) with no basis in the teachings of the Salaf (early Muslims) and no imam held it. The author dismisses this objection as false and born of ignorance of the actual schools of the Salaf. To prove this, the author cites Imam Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi, a highly respected Hanafi scholar (d. 321 AH), whose knowledge of the Salaf's sayings and especially the sayings of Abu Hanifa's followers is well known. Tahawi's book al-'Aqa'id (The Creeds) begins with a statement that the doctrine he presents is that of the jurists: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani. Although the quote is cut off, it is clear that Tahawi attributes this creed—which includes the eternity of takwin—to the founding imams of the Hanafi school, thus demonstrating that the view has authentic Salaf precedent.

Refuting the Claim of Innovation: The Salaf on Eternal Attributes
Nasafi refutes the objection by quoting Tahawi's creedal statement affirming eternal divine attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses the authority of Imam al-Tahawi and the early Hanafi school to refute the accusation that affirming the eternity of takwin is a later innovation.

Core Idea
The eternity of takwin is not an innovation but the doctrine of the earliest imams.

Nasafi now addresses a key objection: that the view of takwin as an eternal attribute has no basis in the Salaf and is a later innovation. To refute this, he does not rely on rational argument alone but appeals to the written testimony of one of the most authoritative Hanafi scholars, Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi, whose creedal work explicitly affirms that Allah's attributes—including the meaning of creatorness—are eternal, even when no creatures exist. This lesson examines how Nasafi uses this quotation to establish continuity with early orthodoxy.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Notice the structure: Nasafi first dismisses the objection then provides textual evidence.
2
Identify the objection and its refutation
Pinpoint the specific claim made by the opponents and how Nasafi characterizes it.
The opponents claim the view is an innovation (hadath) with no Salaf precedent.
3
Examine the Tahawi quote
Study the excerpt from al-'Aqa'id and understand what it affirms about Allah's attributes before creation.
Tahawi says Allah has never ceased to be with His attributes, and has the meaning of lordship and creatorness even without creatures.
4
Analyze Nasafi's interpretation
See how Nasafi unpacks Tahawi's words to show they support the eternity of the attribute of creation.
5
Appreciate the force of the argument
Understand why appealing to early authority is rhetorically powerful in this context.
Nasafi concludes that the view was held by Abu Hanifa and his companions, so it cannot be a later innovation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول لهم: لو لم يكن ما ذكرنا من وجوب وجود التكوين قائما بذات الباري في الأزل، كان ثبوت الإمكان كافيا لتعينه للثبوت، ودليل الإمكان دفع ما ذكرتم من الشبه وكلها مندفعة فاسدة. ولابد من أن نشتغل ببيان بطلانها في أنفسها فنقول: أما ما زعموا أن هذا القول حادث لا أصل له في السلف ولا قائل به من الأئمة، فقول باطل صدر عن الجهل بمذاهب السلف، وذلك أن أبا جعفر الطحاوي وهو مما لا تخفى درجته وعلو رتبته في معرفة أقاويل سلف الأمة على العموم ومعرفة أقاويل أصحاب أبي حنيفة على الخصوص قال في كتابه المسمى بالعقائد الذي افتتحه فقال: صح عندي مذهب فقهاء الملة أبي حنيفة النعمان بن ثابت الكوفي وأبي يوسف يعقوب بن إبراهيم الأنصاري وأبي عبد الله محمد بن الحسن الشيباني ثم شرع في بيان أقاويلهم إلى أن قال: وما زال بصفاته قديما قبل خلقه ولم يزدد بكونهم شيئا لم يكن قبلهم من صفته ثم قال: له معنى الربوبية ولا مربوب ومعنى الخالقية ولا مخلوق، وأراد بقوله: قبل خلقه أي قبل مخلوقاته، ألا ترى أنه قال: ولم يزدد بكونهم شيئا ولم يقل بكونه، ولأنه لو أراد به صفة الخلق لم يقل لم يزدد، وفي هذا أيضا إشارة إلى الدليل في المسألة، بينا أنه لا يجوز أن يستفيد بالمخلوقين صفة مدح. وإن قولا كان أبو حنيفة وكبار أصحابه قائلين به مع تبحرهم في أنواع العلوم وتقدم زمانهم، لحقيق أن لا ينسب إلى الحدوث بعد الأربعمائة من سني الهجرة وجهالة من نسبه إلى ذلك ظاهرة. ثم إن أئمة أصحاب أبي حنيفة السالكين طريقه في الأصول والفروع، الناكبين عن
Then we say to them: If what we mentioned of the necessity of the existence of takwin subsisting in the essence of the Creator in pre-eternity did not exist, then the establishment of possibility would be sufficient for its determination for affirmation, and the proof of possibility repels what you mentioned of specious arguments, all of which are repelled and invalid. And we must engage in explaining their falsehood in themselves, so we say: As for their claim that this statement is an innovation with no root in the Salaf and no one among the imams said it, it is a false statement arising from ignorance of the doctrines of the Salaf. That is because Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi—whose rank and high station in knowing the sayings of the Salaf of the Ummah in general and knowing the sayings of the companions of Abu Hanifa in particular are not hidden—said in his book called al-'Aqa'id, which he opened by saying: 'The doctrine of the jurists of the religion, Abu Hanifa al-Nu'man ibn Thabit al-Kufi, Abu Yusuf Ya'qub ibn Ibrahim al-Ansari, and Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, has become sound to me.' Then he began to explain their sayings until he said: 'And He has never ceased to be with His attributes eternally before His creation, and He did not increase by their becoming something that was not of His attribute before them.' Then he said: 'He has the meaning of lordship while there is no lord, and the meaning of creatorness while there is no created being.' And he meant by his saying 'before His creation' that is, before His creatures. Do you not see that he said 'and He did not increase by their becoming something' and did not say 'by His becoming'? And because if he meant the attribute of creation, he would not say 'He did not increase.' And in this there is also an indication of the proof in the issue: we have shown that it is not permissible for Him to acquire an attribute of praise from creatures. And that a statement that Abu Hanifa and his senior companions held, with their deep knowledge in types of sciences and the precedence of their time, is truly not to be attributed to innovation after four hundred years of the Hijra, and the ignorance of one who attributes it to that is apparent. Then indeed the imams of the companions of Abu Hanifa who follow his path in principles and branches, who deviate from...
Source pages p. 554

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection raised against the view that takwin (bringing into existence) is an eternal attribute subsisting in God's essence. The objectors claimed that this opinion is an innovation (hadath) with no basis in the Salaf and that no imam held it. The author responds by quoting Imam Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi, a prominent Hanafi authority, from his work al-'Aqa'id. Tahawi explicitly states that Allah has never ceased to be with His attributes eternally before creation, and that He has the meaning of lordship (rububiyya) and creatorness (khaliqiyya) even when no creature exists. The author then interprets Tahawi's words to show that they affirm the eternity of the attribute of creation (khalq/takwin) without it being dependent on the existence of created beings. He concludes that this view was held by Abu Hanifa and his senior companions, who were early scholars, and therefore it cannot be dismissed as a later innovation. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the argument is clear: the charge of innovation is baseless and stems from ignorance of the Salaf's doctrines.

Key Terms
حادث
سلف
أئمة
طحاوي
ربوبية
خالقية
تكوين
صفة الخلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the doctrine of takwin as an eternal attribute was introduced after the Salaf and has no basis in early Islam.
Correction: Nasafi shows that Tahawi, a prominent early Hanafi scholar, explicitly affirmed that Allah has the meaning of creatorness from eternity, and this was the view of Abu Hanifa and his companions.

Checkpoint
How does Nasafi refute the claim that the eternity of takwin is an innovation?
A) By presenting a rational proof only
B) By quoting Tahawi's creed which affirms Allah's attributes eternally before creation
C) By citing a verse from the Quran
D) By arguing that all later scholars agree

Key Takeaway
Nasafi defends the eternity of takwin by demonstrating that it is not an innovation but the established teaching of Abu Hanifa and his early followers, as recorded by Tahawi.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a theological claim that seems new to you, do you immediately doubt it, or do you investigate whether the earliest Muslims held it? What does your reaction say about the depth of your connection to the Salaf?
?
You believe in Allah's attributes, but do you truly live as if His attributes—like His Power and Ability to create—are eternal and not dependent on your existence? If you felt the weight of His eternal creatorness right now, what would change in how you face today's tasks?
?
The lesson shows that even great scholars like Tahawi dedicated themselves to preserving the exact words of the imams. What area of your faith have you taken for granted without checking its authenticity from the sources? Make a firm resolve to verify one belief this week.

Spread of I'tizal in Transoxiana and Khurasan
Describes the widespread presence of I'tizal in Transoxiana and Khurasan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that I'tizal was the dominant madhhab in Transoxiana and Khurasan in ancient times before the Maturidi school.

Core Idea
Before Maturidism, I'tizal dominated Transoxiana and Khurasan.

This passage provides a historical snapshot showing that the Mu'tazili school was prevalent in the regions of Transoxiana and Khurasan, including major cities like Marw and Balkh. It sets the stage for understanding the environment in which the Maturidi school later emerged.

Guided Path
1
Read the historical statement
Read the Arabic and translation to understand the claim that I'tizal was in all lands of Transoxiana and Khurasan.
Note the cities named: Marw and Balkh.
2
Interpret 'in ancient times'
Consider why the author specifies 'in ancient times' — this indicates a historical shift.
This sets up the need for the Maturidi response.
3
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: How does knowing this context help in understanding the rise of Maturidism?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاعتزال في جميع ديار ما وراء النهر وخراسان من مرو وبلخ وغيرهما، كلهم في قديم الزمان كانوا على هذا المذهب، وأئمتنا بسمرقند الجامعون علم الأصول والفروع الذابون عن حريم الدين المناضلون عنه الذين طهر الله تعالى بسبب غزارة علومهم وتبحرهم في علم الكلام، وصلابتهم في الدين، وتشددهم على أهل البدع والضلال الذين صانوا أهل هذه الديار عن أوضار أهل الزيغ والبدع عامة، كانوا على هذا الرأي من لدن أيام الشيخ أبي بكر أحمد بن إسحاق بن صبيح الجوزجاني صاحب أبي سليمان الجوزجاني تلميذ محمد بن الحسن، وكان في أنواع العلوم على الخصوص والعموم في الذروة العالية والرتبة السامية، ومن رأى تصانيفه ككتاب الفرق والتمييز وكتاب التوبة وغيرهما عرف جلالة قدرة إلى زماننا هذا.
I'tizal was in all the lands of Transoxiana and Khurasan, from Marw and Balkh and others; all of them in ancient times were upon this madhhab. And our imams in Samarkand, those who gathered the science of principles (usul) and branches (furu'), the defenders of the sanctity of the religion, the fighters for it, those whom Allah purified due to the abundance of their sciences and their deep knowledge in the science of kalam, and their firmness in religion, and their severity against the people of innovation and misguidance, who protected the people of these lands from the defilements of the people of deviation and innovation generally, were upon this opinion since the days of Sheikh Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ishaq ibn Subayh al-Juzjani, the companion of Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani, the student of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan. And he was in the types of sciences, both specific and general, at the highest peak and the most sublime rank. And whoever saw his works, like the Book of Sects and Distinction (Kitab al-Furq wa al-Tamyiz) and the Book of Repentance (Kitab al-Tawba) and others, would know the grandeur of his status up to our time.
Source pages p. 556

Commentary
This passage is a historical narrative describing the religious landscape of Transoxiana and Khurasan before the rise of the Maturidi school. It states that I'tizal (Mu'tazilism) was widespread in all these regions, including Marw, Balkh, and others, in ancient times. Then it highlights the role of the Maturidi imams of Samarkand, who were masters of both usul (principles of religion) and furu' (positive law). They are described as defenders of the faith, purified by Allah due to their deep knowledge of kalam (dialectical theology) and their severity against ahl al-bid' wa al-dalal (people of innovation and misguidance). They protected the region from the defilements of ahl al-zaygh wa al-bid' (people of deviation and innovation). This tradition dates back to the time of Sheikh Abu Bakr al-Juzjani, who was a companion of Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani, a student of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani. The author then praises Abu Bakr al-Juzjani, noting his high rank in all sciences and the importance of his works such as Kitab al-Furq wa al-Tamyiz and Kitab al-Tawba, which testify to his great stature.

Key Terms

ما وراء النهر
خراسان
مرو

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the Maturidi school was always the majority in Central Asia.
Correction: The passage shows that before Maturidism, I'tizal was prevalent.

Checkpoint

B) I'tizal
C) Ash'arism
D) Hanbalism

Key Takeaway
I'tizal was the dominant madhhab in Transoxiana and Khurasan before the Maturidi school.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Praises the Maturidi imams of Samarkand and highlights Abu Bakr al-Juzjani's works.

Maturidi imams protected Transoxiana from I'tizal through deep knowledge and rigor.

The Antiquity of the Maturidi School: A Historical Defense
Enumerates Maturidi scholars' death dates to refute novelty charge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the timeline of early Maturidi scholars refutes the claim that the school is a recent innovation.

Core Idea
The Maturidi school's early scholars predate al-Ash'ari, proving its antiquity.

In this passage, the author counters the accusation that the Maturidi school is a late invention. He presents a chronological list of early Maturidi imams, showing they died before or around the time of al-Ash'ari. This establishes the school's early roots and exposes the charge as obstinacy.

Guided Path
1
Read the historical argument
Read the Arabic passage focusing on the dates of early Maturidi scholars from Bukhara, Transoxiana, Merv, and Balkh.
Notice the author mentions scholars dying before 300 AH and between 300-340 AH.
2
Compare with al-Ash'ari's death
The author gives al-Ash'ari's death year as 324 AH and shows Maturidi scholars were contemporaries or older.
Abu Mansur al-Maturidi died shortly after al-Ash'ari.
3
Understand the rhetorical question
The author asks how the school can be rejected as novel while accepting al-Ash'ari, unless one is obstinate.
This is the key point of the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو استقصيت ذكر من كان على هذا المذهب من أئمة بخاري وجميع ديار ما وراء النهر إلى أقصى ثغور الترك وأئمة مرو وبلخ، وأبنت عن جلالة قدرهم وتبحرهم في أصناف العلوم لطال الكتاب وقصرت عن بلوغ المراد وأكثر من ذكرت من قدماء هؤلاء ماتوا قبل ثلاثمائة، وكثير منهم ماتوا فيما بين ثلاثمائة إلى ثلاثمائة وثلاثين وثلاثمائة وأربعين. ووفاة الأشعري كان في سنة أربع وعشرين وثلاثمائة وتوفي الشيخ أبو منصور بعد وفاة الأشعري بقليل والشيخ أبو القاسم الحكيم فيما أظنه مات سنة خمس وثلاثين وثلاثمائة فهؤلاء كانوا من طبقة الأشعري ومن تقدم من أستاذيهم وأستاذي أستاذيهم ماتوا قبله بزمان طويل. فكيف يرد هذا القول بحدوث العهد ويقبل ما تفوه به الأشعري من الأقاويل بهذا العيب لولا التعنت. هذا أن أكثر رجال الصوفية الذين كانت بحور علومهم زاخرة وكراماتهم مع فيما بين الخلائق ظاهرة كانوا على هذا المذهب، ذكر هذا عنهم الشيخ العالم أبو بكر بن أبي إسحاق الكلاباذي فيما حكى من مذهبهم وعقيدتهم في كتابه المسمى بالتعرف لبيان مذهب التصوف وهو الموثوق به فيما يروي العدل وفيما يحكي ومن عرف سداد طريقته وصفاء عقيدته ونزاهته وصلابته في الدين وأمانته، عرف أنه لا يروي عن أحد شيئا إلا بعد تثبت ويقين واندفاع الشك والريبة، ومذهب كانت
And if I were to enumerate the mention of those who followed this school from the imams of Bukhara and all the lands of Transoxiana to the farthest frontiers of the Turks, and the imams of Merv and Balkh, and expound on the majesty of their rank and their mastery in the various sciences, the book would become long and I would fall short of achieving the desired. Most of those I mentioned among the early ones died before three hundred [AH], and many of them died between three hundred and three hundred and thirty and three hundred and forty. The death of al-Ash'ari was in the year three hundred and twenty-four, and Sheikh Abu Mansur died shortly after the death of al-Ash'ari, and Sheikh Abu al-Qasim al-Hakim, as I suppose, died in the year three hundred and thirty-five. So these were of the class of al-Ash'ari and those who preceded from their teachers and the teachers of their teachers died long before him. So how can this statement be rejected on the basis of newness, and what al-Ash'ari uttered from sayings be accepted with this defect, if not for obstinacy? Furthermore, most of the Sufi men whose seas of knowledge were overflowing and whose miracles were apparent among the creatures were upon this school. This was mentioned about them by the learned sheikh Abu Bakr ibn Abi Ishaq al-Kalabadhi in what he narrated of their school and creed in his book called al-Ta'arruf for explaining the school of Sufism, and he is reliable in what he relates and narrates. And whoever knows the soundness of his way, the purity of his creed, his integrity, his steadfastness in religion, and his trustworthiness, knows that he does not narrate anything about anyone except after verification and certainty and the elimination of doubt and suspicion. And the school was...
Source pages p. 560

Commentary
This passage is a defense of the Maturidi school against the accusation that it is a recent innovation (hadath al-'ahd). The author first mentions that if he were to list all the Maturidi scholars from Khurasan and Transoxiana, the book would be too long. He then provides a chronology: most early Maturidi scholars died before 300 AH, and many between 300 and 340 AH. He corrects the death date of al-Ash'ari (324 AH) and notes that Abu Mansur al-Maturidi died shortly after him, while Abu al-Qasim al-Hakim died around 335 AH. Thus, the early Maturidi scholars were contemporaries of al-Ash'ari, and their teachers predated him. Therefore, it is unreasonable to reject the Maturidi school on grounds of novelty while accepting al-Ash'ari's views, unless one is obstinate. The author then adds that most Sufi scholars adhered to the Maturidi school, citing the reliable Sufi master Abu Bakr al-Kalabadhi and his book 'al-Ta'arruf'. Al-Kalabadhi is described as trustworthy, only narrating after verification, which supports the authenticity of the Maturidi tradition among Sufis.

Key Terms
طبقة الأشعري (tabaqat al-Ash'ari)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Maturidi school is a later development that arose after al-Ash'ari.
Correction: The passage shows that early Maturidi scholars died before or around the same time as al-Ash'ari, indicating the school's antiquity.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when did most early Maturidi scholars die?
A) After 400 AH
B) Before 300 AH
C) Between 300 and 340 AH
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi school has early scholars predating al-Ash'ari, refuting the claim of novelty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The author uses historical evidence to defend a school of thought. Are you willing to examine your own deeply held beliefs with the same honesty, even if it means correcting a long-held assumption?
?
In what areas of your life do you cling to a position out of habit rather than evidence? What concrete step can you take this week to test a belief you hold?

Sufi Support for the Maturidi Creed: The Testimony of al-Kalabadhi
Cites Sufi scholars' adherence to Maturidi school via al-Kalabadhi's trustworthy work.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
Sufi saints adhered to the Maturidi school, and al-Kalabadhi's reliable record proves it.

The author further strengthens his defense by citing the adherence of renowned Sufi scholars to the Maturidi school. He specifically mentions Sheikh Abu Bakr al-Kalabadhi and his authoritative work al-Ta'arruf, known for its reliable transmission of Sufi beliefs. This testimony underscores the deep roots of the Maturidi school within Islamic spirituality.

ولو استقصيت ذكر من كان على هذا المذهب من أئمة بخاري وجميع ديار ما وراء النهر إلى أقصى ثغور الترك وأئمة مرو وبلخ، وأبنت عن جلالة قدرهم وتبحرهم في أصناف العلوم لطال الكتاب وقصرت عن بلوغ المراد وأكثر من ذكرت من قدماء هؤلاء ماتوا قبل ثلاثمائة، وكثير منهم ماتوا فيما بين ثلاثمائة إلى ثلاثمائة وثلاثين وثلاثمائة وأربعين. ووفاة الأشعري كان في سنة أربع وعشرين وثلاثمائة وتوفي الشيخ أبو منصور بعد وفاة الأشعري بقليل والشيخ أبو القاسم الحكيم فيما أظنه مات سنة خمس وثلاثين وثلاثمائة فهؤلاء كانوا من طبقة الأشعري ومن تقدم من أستاذيهم وأستاذي أستاذيهم ماتوا قبله بزمان طويل. فكيف يرد هذا القول بحدوث العهد ويقبل ما تفوه به الأشعري من الأقاويل بهذا العيب لولا التعنت. هذا أن أكثر رجال الصوفية الذين كانت بحور علومهم زاخرة وكراماتهم مع فيما بين الخلائق ظاهرة كانوا على هذا المذهب، ذكر هذا عنهم الشيخ العالم أبو بكر بن أبي إسحاق الكلاباذي فيما حكى من مذهبهم وعقيدتهم في كتابه المسمى بالتعرف لبيان مذهب التصوف وهو الموثوق به فيما يروي العدل وفيما يحكي ومن عرف سداد طريقته وصفاء عقيدته ونزاهته وصلابته في الدين وأمانته، عرف أنه لا يروي عن أحد شيئا إلا بعد تثبت ويقين واندفاع الشك والريبة، ومذهب كانت
And if I were to enumerate the mention of those who followed this school from the imams of Bukhara and all the lands of Transoxiana to the farthest frontiers of the Turks, and the imams of Merv and Balkh, and expound on the majesty of their rank and their mastery in the various sciences, the book would become long and I would fall short of achieving the desired. Most of those I mentioned among the early ones died before three hundred [AH], and many of them died between three hundred and three hundred and thirty and three hundred and forty. The death of al-Ash'ari was in the year three hundred and twenty-four, and Sheikh Abu Mansur died shortly after the death of al-Ash'ari, and Sheikh Abu al-Qasim al-Hakim, as I suppose, died in the year three hundred and thirty-five. So these were of the class of al-Ash'ari and those who preceded from their teachers and the teachers of their teachers died long before him. So how can this statement be rejected on the basis of newness, and what al-Ash'ari uttered from sayings be accepted with this defect, if not for obstinacy? Furthermore, most of the Sufi men whose seas of knowledge were overflowing and whose miracles were apparent among the creatures were upon this school. This was mentioned about them by the learned sheikh Abu Bakr ibn Abi Ishaq al-Kalabadhi in what he narrated of their school and creed in his book called al-Ta'arruf for explaining the school of Sufism, and he is reliable in what he relates and narrates. And whoever knows the soundness of his way, the purity of his creed, his integrity, his steadfastness in religion, and his trustworthiness, knows that he does not narrate anything about anyone except after verification and certainty and the elimination of doubt and suspicion. And the school was...
Source pages p. 560

Commentary
This passage is a defense of the Maturidi school against the accusation that it is a recent innovation (hadath al-'ahd). The author first mentions that if he were to list all the Maturidi scholars from Khurasan and Transoxiana, the book would be too long. He then provides a chronology: most early Maturidi scholars died before 300 AH, and many between 300 and 340 AH. He corrects the death date of al-Ash'ari (324 AH) and notes that Abu Mansur al-Maturidi died shortly after him, while Abu al-Qasim al-Hakim died around 335 AH. Thus, the early Maturidi scholars were contemporaries of al-Ash'ari, and their teachers predated him. Therefore, it is unreasonable to reject the Maturidi school on grounds of novelty while accepting al-Ash'ari's views, unless one is obstinate. The author then adds that most Sufi scholars adhered to the Maturidi school, citing the reliable Sufi master Abu Bakr al-Kalabadhi and his book 'al-Ta'arruf'. Al-Kalabadhi is described as trustworthy, only narrating after verification, which supports the authenticity of the Maturidi tradition among Sufis.

Key Terms
التعرف (al-Ta'arruf)
أبو بكر الكلاباذي (Abu Bakr al-Kalabadhi)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Al-Kalabadhi's trustworthy testimony in al-Ta'arruf confirms that most early Sufis followed the Maturidi school.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Kalabadhi is praised for his sound method and purity of creed. Do you hold yourself to the same standard when you accept religious teachings? Will you examine the sources of your beliefs with equal rigor?
?
If most Sufi saints, whose miracles are apparent, followed the Maturidi school, does that humble your pride? What will you do to align your heart with these righteous predecessors?
?
You have read that al-Kalabadhi's testimony is reliable because of his character. Are you someone whose testimony about Islam would be trusted? What does your life say about the creed you claim to follow?

Refutation of Ash'ari on the Command 'Kun'
Response to Ash'ari claim that the command 'Be' does not necessitate existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi distinction between a command of obligation and a command of creation, and how this distinction refutes the Ash'ari claim that the command 'Be' does not necessitate existence.

Core Idea
A command to create must bring existence, or it is evidence of inability.

This passage recounts a Maturidi response to an Ash'ari opponent who argued that the command 'Kun' (Be) is merely a command like any other, and since commands do not necessarily bring about the commanded thing, its eternity does not imply the eternity of creation. The author refutes this by distinguishing two types of divine command: one that establishes obligation and another that brings about existence. This distinction not only answers the objection but also reveals an inconsistency in the Ash'ari position on eternal commands.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage records a debate with direct speech.
2
Identify the Ash'ari claim
The Ash'ari opponent claims that 'Kun' is a command, and commands do not necessarily entail the existence of the commanded thing. Therefore, the eternity of the command does not prove the eternity of creation.
This is the core objection being refuted.
3
Understand the distinction between two types of command
The author distinguishes between 'command of obligation' (amr ijaab) and 'command of creation' (amr takwin). For obligation, only the obligation itself is necessary, not existence. For creation, existence is the intended consequence; if it does not occur, the command is deficient.
This distinction is the key to the refutation.
4
See how the author turns the argument on the Ash'aris
The author points out that Ash'aris believe God's command of obligation is eternal, yet no one is obligated in eternity. They accept that such a command can be eternal and produce obligation later. By analogy, the command of creation (or takwin) can be eternal and produce existence in time, so the Ash'ari objection fails.
This exposes an inconsistency in their own position.
5
Reflect on the broader implication
This argument shows that divine attributes like takwin (bringing into existence) are eternal and effective, but their effects appear in time. It also safeguards God's ability and wisdom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعتراض أشعري والرد عليه وكانت أتكلم مع بعض الأشعرية وألزمته فصل قوله كن، فزعم أن قوله كن أمر ، وليس من قضية الأمر وجود المأمور به لا محالة، فلا يوجب قدمه قدم المكون فأما التكوين فهو فعل، ومن قضية الفعل وجود المفعول لا محالة. فقلت: إنما لم يكن من قضية الأمر وجود المأمور به إذا كان الأمر أمر إيجاب فلم يجب به إلا ما هو حكمة وهو الوجوب، فأما الوجود فليس من حكمه، فأما الأمر إذا لم يكن أمر إيجاب بل كان أمر تكوين فحكمه التكوين فينبغي أن يوجد حكمه، ألا ترى أن في أمر الإيجاب لو لم يوجد المأمور به لما لزم الأمر نقص لأنه ما أمر ليوجد بل أمر ليجب، وقد ثبت ما أثبته بالأمر، وفي أمر التكوين لو لم يوجد المكون لزمه نقص، لأنه أمر ليوجد ، فلم يثبت ما أثبته بالأمر فكان دليل عجز ، فدل أن هذا الكلام باطل، وأن التكوين يوجب المكون، ومع ذلك لم يحصل المكون في الأزل لما مر . فكذا في التكوين، وأمر التكوين مناقضة للأشعرية لا محيص لهم عنها البتة، وكذا أمر الإيجاب لازم عليهم ، إذ هو أزلي عند الأشعرية ولا وجوب إذ الوجوب ولا إذ وجود لمن يجب عليه محال، فلما جاز الإيجاب فى الأزل ليثبت الوجوب عند وجود المكلف، لماذا لم يجز الإيجاد ليتحقق الوجود عند وجود المكون.
Ash'ari objection and response to it: I was speaking with some Ash'ari and I forced him on the matter of His saying 'Be', so he claimed that His saying 'Be' is a command, and it is not a necessary consequence of the command that the commanded thing exists, so its eternity does not necessitate the eternity of the made thing. As for takwin, it is an act, and it is a necessary consequence of the act that the object of the act exists. So I said: the existence of the commanded thing is not a consequence of the command only when the command is a command of obligation, for only what is wisdom – which is obligation – results from it; as for existence, it is not its consequence. As for when the command is not a command of obligation but a command of creation, its consequence is creation, so its consequence should exist. Do you not see that in the command of obligation, if the commanded thing does not exist, the command suffers no deficiency because it was not commanded to exist but to be obligatory, and what it established by the command has been established; but in the command of creation, if the made thing does not exist, deficiency would be necessary because it was commanded to exist, so what it established by the command has not been established, so it would be evidence of inability. This shows that this speech is false, and that takwin necessitates the made thing, and yet the made thing did not come to be in pre-eternity for the reason already mentioned. So it is with takwin. And the command of creation is a contradiction for the Ash'aris from which they have absolutely no escape. Likewise, the command of obligation is binding on them, since it is eternal according to the Ash'aris, yet there is no obligation when the one obligated does not exist, and it is impossible. So when the command of obligation is permissible in pre-eternity to establish obligation at the existence of the obligated, why is it not permissible to bring into existence to realize existence at the existence of the made thing?
Source pages p. 566

Commentary
This passage recounts a debate with an Ash'ari opponent who distinguished between the command 'Be' (Qul kun) and the attribute of takwin. The opponent claimed that 'Kun' is a command, and commands do not necessarily entail the existence of the commanded thing; thus its eternity does not entail the eternity of the created thing. He further claimed that takwin is an act, and acts necessarily entail their objects. The author responds by differentiating between a command of obligation (amr ijaab) and a command of creation (amr takwin). For a command of obligation, the only necessary consequence is the obligation itself, not the existence of the commanded thing. But for a command of creation, the purpose is to bring about existence; if the created thing does not exist, the command is deficient. Therefore, the Ash'ari's analogy fails. The author then points out an inconsistency in the Ash'ari position: they hold that God's command of obligation is eternal, yet there is no one obligated in eternity. If they accept that such a command can be eternal and produce obligation at the appropriate time, then similarly, the command of creation (or takwin) can be eternal and produce existence at the appropriate time. This refutes their objection.

Key Terms
كن
الأمر
التكوين
الإيجاب
المكون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The command 'Be' (Kun) is just like a human command that does not necessarily bring about its object.
Correction: The command 'Be' is a command of creation, not of obligation; its purpose is to bring about existence, so if the object does not appear, the command would be deficient and indicate inability. Thus it necessarily brings about existence.

Checkpoint
How does the author differentiate between a command of obligation and a command of creation?
A) A command of obligation necessitates existence, while a command of creation does not.
B) A command of creation necessitates existence, while a command of obligation only necessitates obligation.
C) Both types of command necessitate existence of the commanded thing.
D) Neither type necessitates existence.

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi refutation hinges on the distinction between commands that obligate and commands that create; the latter necessarily bring about existence, otherwise God would be unable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you ask God for something and don't see it happen immediately, do you really believe that His command 'Be' is always effective, or do you let doubt creep in because you expect a human-like delay? How can you remind yourself that His creative command is not like human commands, and that His timing is part of the perfection of His act?
?
God's command for you to pray is a command of obligation. Do you treat it merely as a box to check, or do you expect that His command actually creates something in your soul? If you believe it is a command of creation as well, how would your prayer change?
?
The Ash'ari in this passage argued that the command 'Be' doesn't necessitate existence. If you ever rationalize that God's promises might not come true because of some theological nuance, look at your own heart: are you hiding behind intellectual arguments to avoid trusting God's absolute power to bring about what He has commanded or promised? What step can you take today to align your expectation with the reality of His takwin?

Irāda and Mashī'a: One Attribute or Two?
Imam al-Nasafi states the synonymity of irāda and mashī'a and refutes the Karramiyya view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that irāda (will) and mashī'a (volition) are synonymous attributes in mainstream Sunni theology, and how the Karramiyya sect deviates from this view.

Core Idea
Irāda and mashī'a are two names for the same eternal attribute.

Imam al-Nasafi now addresses a subtle but important point: whether Allah's will (irāda) and His volition (mashī'a) are the same or different. The majority of theologians affirm their identity, but a small sect called the Karramiyya held a different view. Let's see how the author presents and refutes their position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the clear statement of synonymity and the exception.
2
Identify the majority position
The passage states that irāda and mashī'a are two terms indicating one meaning according to the theologians (mutakallimūn). Understand that this is the normative view.
There is no distinction made by anyone except the Karramiyya.
3
Understand the Karramiyya distinction
The Karramiyya claim that mashī'a is eternal, single, and encompasses all that Allah wills, while irāda is temporal (ḥāditha), multiple, and occurs just before the willed object.
They treat irāda as a created accident in Allah's essence, which is a major deviation.
4
Note the author's rejection
Imam al-Nasafi ends with 'exalted is Allah above that, greatly' (تعالى الله عن ذلك علوا كبيرا), showing strong disapproval of the Karramiyya view.
This indicates that the correct belief is the synonymity of the two attributes.
5
Reflect on the theological importance
Why does this matter? Attributing temporality to Allah's will compromises His perfection and eternity. The consensus on synonymity safeguards tawḥīd.
This is a classic refutation of a sectarian innovation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهي بعينها المشيئة عند المتكلمين. فالإرادة والمشيئة عندهم لفظان ينبئان عن معنى واحد لم يفرق بينهما أحد من المتكلمين إلا الكرامية، فإنهم يزعمون أن المشيئة صفة الله تعالى أزلية وهى صفة واحدة تتناول ما يشاء الله بها من حيث حدث، فأما الإرادة فهي غير المشيئة وهي عندهم حادثه في ذات القديم تعالى الله عن ذلك علوا كبيرا - وله إرادات كثيرة على عداد المرادات يحدث كل إرادة منها قبل حدوث ما هو المراد به، ثم يتعقبها حدوث ما هو المراد بها.
And it is itself mashī'a according to the theologians. For irāda and mashī'a are, in their view, two terms that indicate one and the same meaning; no one among the theologians distinguishes between them except the Karramiyya. For they claim that mashī'a is an attribute of Allah Most High, eternal, and it is one attribute that encompasses whatever Allah wills by means of it in terms of what occurs. As for irāda, it is other than mashī'a, and in their view it is temporal (ḥāditha) in the essence of the Pre-Eternal—exalted is Allah above that, greatly—and He has many irādas corresponding to the number of things willed (murādāt); each irāda occurs before the occurrence of what is willed by it, and then the occurrence of what is willed by it follows it.
Source pages p. 578

Commentary
This passage clarifies the relationship between the two terms irāda (will) and mashī'a (volition). It states that according to the majority of theologians (mutakallimūn), these two terms are synonymous and refer to a single attribute. The only exception is the Karramiyya sect, who distinguish between them. The Karramiyya hold that mashī'a is an eternal, single attribute of Allah that relates to whatever He wills in terms of temporal events. In contrast, irāda is a different attribute that is temporal (ḥāditha) and multiple, each one coming into existence just before the thing willed, after which the willed thing occurs. The author rejects this view with the phrase 'exalted is Allah above that, greatly,' indicating strong disapproval. Thus, the normative Sunni position is that irāda and mashī'a are identical as one eternal attribute.

Key Terms
المشيئة
الإرادة
الكلامية
أزلية
حادثة
المرادات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think irāda and mashī'a are different attributes in Sunni theology.
Correction: The passage shows they are synonymous according to all theologians except the Karramiyya, who are refuted.

Checkpoint
Which group distinguishes between irāda and mashī'a according to this passage?
A) The Mu'tazila.
B) The Ash'aris.
C) The Karramiyya.
D) The Māturīdiyya.

Key Takeaway
In Sunni theology, irāda and mashī'a are one eternal attribute, contrary to the Karramiyya who split them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'if Allah wills' (inshā'Allah), do you truly believe that His will is one and eternal, or do you sometimes imagine that He 'changes His mind'? How does this lesson challenge your hidden assumptions about God's will?
?
The Karramiyya claimed that Allah's irāda is temporal and multiple. Have you ever acted as if Allah's will is reactive to your choices, rather than being a single eternal decree? How can you train your heart to submit to an unchanging divine will?
?
Knowing that the majority of theologians confirm irāda and mashī'a are one attribute, what would you say to someone who believes that Allah's will is fragmented or evolving? Are you prepared to defend this truth with conviction?

Three Theological Definitions of Wisdom (Hikma)
Three definitions of wisdom (ḥikma) from Ash‘ari, Mu‘tazili, and Maturidi schools.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinct definitions of wisdom (ḥikma) and folly (safah) according to the Ash‘ari, Mu‘tazili, and Maturidi schools, and the key differences in their criteria.

Core Idea
Wisdom is defined differently: intention (Ash‘ari), benefit (Mu‘tazili), or outcome (Maturidi).

Theologians debated the true nature of wisdom (al-ḥikma) and its opposite, folly (al-safah). This passage from Imam Nasafi’s Tabsirat al-Adilla concisely presents the definitions of three major theological schools: the Ash‘aris, the Mu‘tazila, and the Maturidis. Understanding these definitions is crucial for grasping later debates on divine action and moral reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping. Then read the English translation. Let the author's own words introduce each school's view.
Notice that the passage is a single sentence listing three distinct views.
2
Identify each school's definition
Find the definition for each school: Ash‘ari, Mu‘tazili, and Maturidi. Note the key Arabic term each uses to define wisdom.
The Ash‘ari use 'qaṣd' (intention), the Mu‘tazila use 'naf‘' (benefit), and the Maturidis use 'al-‘āqiba al-ḥamīda' (praiseworthy outcome).
3
Compare the three criteria
Compare the definitions: how do intention, benefit, and outcome differ? Which one is about the action itself, its effects, or its end result?
This comparison sets the stage for deeper kalam discussions on divine actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما الحكمة على رأي المتكلمين فزعم الأشعري أن الحكمة في الفعل وقوعه على قصد فاعله والسفه وقوعه على خلاف قصد فاعله. وقالت المعتزلة الحكمة كل فعل فيه نفع إما للفاعل وإما لغير الفاعل والسفه كل فعل خلا عن المنفعة إما للفاعل وإما لغير الفاعل. وعندنا الحكمة ما له عاقبة حميدة، والسفه ما خلا عن العاقبة الحميدة، والكلام في بيان الصحيح من هذه الأقاويل والفاسد منها يطول جدا إذ له شعب
As for wisdom (al-ḥikma) according to the opinion of the theologians: Al-Ash‘arī claimed that wisdom in action is its occurrence according to the intention of the agent, and folly (al-safah) is its occurrence contrary to the intention of the agent. The Mu‘tazila said: Wisdom is every action in which there is benefit either for the agent or for someone other than the agent, and folly is every action devoid of benefit either for the agent or for someone other than the agent. And according to us: Wisdom is that which has a praiseworthy outcome (al-‘āqiba al-ḥamīda), and folly is that which is devoid of a praiseworthy outcome. And the discourse explaining the correct of these statements and the false is very lengthy, for it has many branches.
Source pages p. 589

Commentary
This passage presents a classification of three theological definitions of wisdom (ḥikma) and folly (safah). The author first states that according to the theologians, there are three main views. The Ash‘ari school defines wisdom as an action that occurs in accordance with the agent's intention (qaṣd); folly is an action contrary to the agent's intention. The Mu‘tazili school defines wisdom as an action that contains benefit (naf‘) for the agent or another; folly is an action devoid of benefit. The Maturidi school (noted by 'according to us') defines wisdom as that which has a praiseworthy outcome (al-‘āqiba al-ḥamīda); folly is that which lacks such an outcome. The author notes that a detailed discussion of which view is correct and which incorrect would be very lengthy due to many ramifications. The passage thus provides a concise summary of the three major definitions, highlighting the key differences: intention (Ash‘ari), benefit (Mu‘tazili), and outcome (Maturidi).

Key Terms
حكمة
سفه
قصد
نفع
عاقبة حميدة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All schools define wisdom in the same way.
Correction: This passage shows they differ fundamentally: Ash‘ari uses intention, Mu‘tazili uses benefit, and Maturidi uses outcome as the criterion.

Checkpoint
According to the Maturidi school, what is the definition of wisdom (al-ḥikma)?
A) An action that benefits the agent
B) An action that occurs according to the agent's intention
C) That which has a praiseworthy outcome
D) An action that is morally good

Key Takeaway
The three schools define wisdom based on different criteria: intention (Ash‘ari), benefit (Mu‘tazili), and outcome (Maturidi), reflecting broader theological differences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you evaluate your daily decisions, which definition of wisdom do you instinctively use—are you most concerned with your intention, the benefit to yourself or others, or the ultimate outcome? How might your default standard miss the deeper wisdom that God expects of you?
?
The Maturidi definition ties wisdom to a praiseworthy outcome. Is there an area of your life where you are avoiding acting wisely because you cannot see a positive outcome, even though you know God promises a good end for the righteous? What is one step you can take this week to trust in that promise and act with faith?
?
Consider a moment you acted with what you thought was wisdom, but later questioned its value. Which school's definition would judge that action differently? If God's wisdom is not merely your intention or the immediate benefit, how does that challenge you to seek a deeper, more faithful standard for your actions?
